## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of concentration dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t, which is the fundamental problem of chemical kinetics rate law identification. The rate typically depends on powers of concentration, and time-dependence may arise from external forcing, autocatalysis, or coupled reactions where other species have been eliminated.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (radioactive decay, unimolecular decomposition)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction with single species)
- General n-th order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (fractional or arbitrary reaction order)
- Mixed first-order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (first-order with constant production/source term)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (approach to equilibrium, A_eq = c1*c2)
- Michaelis-Menten / saturation kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction)
- Autocatalytic rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis)
- Second-order with linear term: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 + c1 * A (competing first and second order pathways)
- Time-dependent first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate constant, e.g., temperature ramp)
- Polynomial rate law: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A + c2 * A**2 + c3 * A**3 (complex multi-step mechanism)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Power-law with time modulation: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * t**c2 (fractal or anomalous kinetics)
- Cooperative/Hill-type kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (cooperative binding/reaction)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA/dt is proportional to A^n, plotting log|dA/dt| vs log|A| yields a straight line with slope n (reaction order identification)
- A rate law independent of A (zero-order) often indicates a saturated catalyst or surface-limited process
- Quadratic dependence on A (A*(c-A) form) suggests autocatalytic or logistic growth mechanisms common in oscillating reactions
- Rational forms A/(K+A) indicate enzymatic or surface-adsorption-limited kinetics (Langmuir-Hinshelwood mechanism)
- Explicit time dependence in the rate law suggests non-isothermal conditions, photochemical initiation, or elimination of coupled species
- Negative dA/dt with positive A indicates consumption (reactant), while positive dA/dt indicates production or autocatalysis
- Cubic terms in A (A^3) may arise from termolecular steps or reduced mechanisms of complex reaction networks
- If the rate law contains both positive and negative terms in A, this indicates competing formation and consumption pathways (reversible or parallel reactions)
